  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>I have a table with a long integer primary key field and 11 million rows. I seem to be unable to load large chunks of rows via id in a reasonably efficient manner.</p> 
                  <p> 1. If I do individual lookups via the primary key, then a fast indexed lookup occurs. However, if I do large numbers of such queries, then the time is overwhelmed by round-trip overhead which makes everything incredibly slow.</p> 
                  <p> 2. If I use a single query with a disjunction of the primary keys of interest, then a table scan is performed (even if the clause only contains 1-3 items), which walks over 11 million rows...incredibly inefficient.</p> 
                  <p> 3. If I use an IN clause, then a table scan is performed (even if the clause only contains 1-3 items), which walks over 11 million rows...incredibly inefficient.</p> 
                  <p>I'm guessing that this might have something to do with the fact that I'm using large integers and really big numbers that don't start anywhere at or about 1 for my keys. Could this possibly be confusing the optimizer?</p> 
                  <p>Here are the unlimited query plans for the 3 cases that I enumerated:<br> *********************************************************************************************</p> 
                  <p><span class="error">[EL Fine]</span>: 2013-01-17 11:09:53.384-<del>ServerSession(582235416)</del><del>Connection(1430986883)</del><del>Thread(Thread<span class="error">["Initial Lisp Listener",5,SubL Thread Group]</span>)</del>-SELECT TERM_ID, ARG0, ARG1, ARG2, ARG3, FORMULA_HASH, FORMULA_LENGTH, FORMULA_TYPE, KB_STATUS FROM KB.FORMULA_TERM WHERE (TERM_ID = ?)<br> bind =&gt; <span class="error">[2251799814033500]</span></p>

                  <p> constructor time (milliseconds) = 0<br> open time (milliseconds) = 0<br> next time (milliseconds) = 0<br> close time (milliseconds) = 0<br> optimizer estimated row count: 1.00<br> optimizer estimated cost: 6.59<br> Index Scan ResultSet for FORMULA_TERM using constraint KB_FORMULA_TERM_TERM_ID_PK at read committed isolation level using share row locking chosen by the optimizer<br> Number of opens = 1<br> Rows seen = 1<br> Rows filtered = 0<br> Fetch Size = 1<br> constructor time (milliseconds) = 0<br> open time (milliseconds) = 0<br> next time (milliseconds) = 0<br> close time (milliseconds) = 0<br> next time in milliseconds/row = 0</p>

class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI just tried it with regular integers, starting from 1 and the only indexing being the primary key. Still get the same issue. If I make a table with 64 rows, then it does fast b-tree scans using the IN query. If the table has 256 or more rows, it does slow heap scans over every row in the table when using the IN query. It looks like maybe there is a logic-po in the code. Doing full table scans over small tables might be faster than multi-probing, but instead it is doing it on large tables. This is just a wild guess.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHere is the SQL:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eDROP TABLE VARIABLE_TERM;\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eCREATE TABLE VARIABLE_TERM\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n(\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        term_id                  INTEGER NOT NULL,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        var_name              VARCHAR(1024) NOT NULL,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n title=\'18\\/Jan\\/13 22:53\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-01-18T22:53:29+0000\'\u003e18\\/Jan\\/13 22:53\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I just tried it with regular integers, starting from 1 and the only indexing being the primary key. Still get the same issue. If I make a table with 64 rows, then it does fast b-tree scans using the IN query. If the table has 256 or more rows, it does slow heap scans over every row in the table when using the IN query. It looks like maybe there is a logic-po in the code. Doing full table scans over small tables might be faster than multi-probing, but instead it is doing it on large tables. This is just a wild guess. \\n\\n Here is the SQL: \\n\\n DROP TABLE VARIABLE_TERM; \\n\\n CREATE TABLE VARIABLE_TERM \\n( \\n        term_id                  INTEGER NOT NULL, \\n        var_name              VARCHAR(1024) NOT NULL, \\n        var_type                SMALLINT NOT NULL,      \\n        kb_status              INTEGER NOT NULL         \\n); If you take your breakpoint of 25 and multiply by 8 you get 200 which is roughly around the breakpoint that I\'m seeing.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-13571092\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-6045?focusedCommentId=13571092&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-13571092\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"mamtas\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13571092_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=mamtas\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"mamtas\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Mamta A. In your case you have 32k pages and your test data looks like it is something like ~20 bytes per row (just a guess from the datatypes\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nand that varchar only takes up the necessary room). I think what mamta\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nis seeing now is, in all cases run update statistics after data is loaded and before queries are executed:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e10.9 - 10 rows index scan, 24 rows table scan , 10k rows index scan\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n10.8 through 10.3 - 10 rows index scan, 24 rows table scan, 10k rows test not tried, but assume it will pick index scan\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAt the low number of rows end if you just look at costs it may make perfect sense from just a cycle cost perspective to choose a table scan\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nvs. using index.   The reason for this is that I\\/O cost dominates over the cost to scan every row on a page.  So in the case where the base\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntable has 1 page and the index has 1 page, pure costing will often choose to scan the 1 data page rather than pay 1 i\\/o to get index page and\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthen another i\\/o to get data page.  For other reasons (mostly to not have to lock all the rows you see during a table scan) the derby code has been \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nchanged to fudge the costs a little to get index scans chosen \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nin this case, most notably a single probe query using with an exact key match using an index.  These fixes tend to aplly only to low number of \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nrows anomaly\'s, and not to the real life issues like your 11 million row case.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"mikem\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13578786_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=mikem\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"mikem\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Mike Matrigali\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13578786_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/Feb\\/13 22:59\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-02-14T22:59:03+0000\'\u003e14\\/Feb\\/13 22:59\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Tony, at least for the int test that mamta has added we are seeing index scan used for 10k rows. The commit comments were as follows\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n****************************************************\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-6045\\\" title=\\\"in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-6045\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-6045\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e (in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eChanges for \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-3790\\\" title=\\\"Investigate if request for update statistics can be skipped for certain kind of indexes, one instance may be unique indexes based on one column.\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-3790\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-3790\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e (Investigate if request for update statistics can be skipped for certain kind of indexes, one instance may be unique indexes based on one column.) caused Derby to use table scan rather than index scan since we do not generate stats for single column unique index. As part of that change, we forgot to make code changes in optimizer to compensate for missing stats for such indexes. As found in \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-6045\\\" title=\\\"in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-6045\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-6045\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e (in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows), even though we do not keep the statistics for single-column unique indexes, we should improve the selectivity of such an index when the index is being considered by the optimizer.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eMaking the relevant code changes now allows us to enable the tests in InListMultiProbeTest.java since they will now run correctly by picking up index scan rather than table scan.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAdditionally, one test in refActions1.sql does not have order by to it and there are only 3 rows in the table. Without the changes for \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/DERBY-6045\\\" title=\\\"in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"DERBY-6045\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eDERBY-6045\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e we were using index scan for it but now it uses table scan which is giving the rows in different order. I have added order by to the query so plan selection does not change order of the rows. The reason behind table scan might be that with only 3 rows in the table, it is cheaper to do table sccan rather than index scan. \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n****************************************************\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"mamtas\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13619507_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=mamtas\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"mamtas\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Mamta A. Satoor\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13619507_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Apr\\/13 04:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-02T04:33:39+0000\'\u003e02\\/Apr\\/13 04:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Committed changes for this jira with revision 1463378. The commit comments were as follows \\n**************************************************** \\n  DERBY-6045   (in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows) \\n\\n Changes for   DERBY-3790   (Investigate if request for update statistics can be skipped for certain kind of indexes, one instance may be unique indexes based on one column.) caused Derby to use table scan rather than index scan since we do not generate stats for single column unique index. As part of that change, we forgot to make code changes in optimizer to compensate for missing stats for such indexes. As found in   DERBY-6045   (in list multi-probe by primary key not chosen on tables with &gt;256 rows), even though we do not keep the statistics for single-column unique indexes, we should improve the selectivity of such an index when the index is being considered by the optimizer. \\n\\n Making the relevant code changes now allows us to enable the tests in InListMultiProbeTest.java since they will now run correctly by picking up index scan rather than table scan. \\n\\n Additionally, one test in refActions1.sql does not have order by to it and there are only 3 rows in the table. Without the changes for   DERBY-6045   we were using index scan for it but now it uses table scan which is giving the rows in different order. I have added order by to the query so plan selection does not change order of the rows. The reason behind table scan might be that with only 3 rows in the table, it is cheaper to do table sccan rather than index scan.  \\n****************************************************
